National Federation of Commerce Cables Legislative Yuan to Request Prompt Amendment of Civil Code Partnership Articles

Expedite Responsible Parties to Address Numerous Abuses, Hoping for Swift Remediation to Maintain Commerce

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce yesterday cabled the Legislative Yuan, again requesting the amendment of Article 681 of the Civil Code, stating: "It is noted that during the National Industry and Commerce Conference in the 19th year of the Republic, our Federation, citing the Civil Code's provisions on partnership business and the attendant responsibility issues, which were causing obstacles, earnestly requested that supplementary articles be deliberated and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for remedy. The proposal was submitted to the Industry and Commerce Conference, and Representative Li Kuan was tasked with presenting it to the conference for review. It was deemed valid and included as Case No. 81, submitted to the conference for discussion. After Li Kuan reported on the reasons and methods for the case, Chairman Kong Xiangxi solemnly reported, stating, 'As chairman, I have previously argued vehemently against joint liability during political and state council meetings, but did not receive support due to the lack of agreement at the time. This conference consists of national industry and commerce leaders and experts discussing the direction of industry and commerce. Since Sichuan has this proposition, and the situation is similar in other regions, let us discuss it thoroughly and submit it to the government for amendment or supplementation.' Member Pan Xulun also stated that joint liability hinders business, citing the closure of Shanghai money houses as an example, and requested supplementary unlimited liability companies for relief. Member Zhang Xiangshi also seconded the motion. Chairman Kong proposed that the case regarding unlimited liability companies be forwarded to the Legislative Yuan through the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for consideration. A majority voted in favor of the proposal. Last year, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce noted that partnership is the most common form of business organization in our country, apart from sole proprietorships. Recently, with the power of the Mixed Court in foreign hands, Chinese-foreign litigation cases have led to joint liability being imposed on partnership debts, causing great uproar and years of dispute. Consequently, those with ample capital have hesitated to invest. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce then requested that your esteemed court amend the legal precedents for joint liability in partnership debts. However, the amendment of Article 681 of the Civil Code and the supplementary addition of articles on unlimited liability companies have not yet been promulgated. Public sentiment is eagerly awaiting this. In recent years, commerce in various regions has continued to decline, largely because those with some capital are wary of partnerships, fearing potential bankruptcy and ruin. Consequently, existing businesses are gradually closing, and new businesses are rare. In this time of commercial decline, things are becoming even more desolate, with the situation worsening daily. Unless promptly remedied, the consequences are dire. Joint liability has many drawbacks, and adding unlimited liability companies is essential. This type of company involves unlimited liability based on shares, which aligns well with the actual practices and customs in Chongqing and other regions. We earnestly request that supplementary articles be added to the current Civil Code's debt section, stipulating that in partnership businesses with unlimited liability based on shares, if the partnership assets are insufficient to settle partnership debts, each partner shall bear responsibility for the shortfall proportionally according to their shares. This would help to remedy the commercial situation. In addition to recommending several executive committee members, including Li Kuan, the former representative to the National Industry and Commerce Conference, to directly submit the request, we are also requesting your esteemed association to forward the amendment. Respectfully, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce.

News from Chongming and Chuansha on Disaster Relief

Chuansha

A storm surge on Hengsha Island, Chuansha County, caused a disaster, with people and livestock swept away. Approximately two thousand households and seven thousand people were affected. The situation is extremely dire. County Magistrate Li, together with local gentry Huang Renzhi, Zhang Bochu, and Lu Wenmei, organized a disaster relief association, establishing thirty fundraising teams to solicit donations from all sides. The team leaders are working diligently, and philanthropists are generously contributing. In recent days, the association has dispatched personnel with one thousand silver dollars and several hundred piculs of rice and wheat to the disaster area for emergency relief, and purchased over thirty thousand catties of rice straw to distribute to affected households for building temporary shelters. The Standing Committee of the association decided to advance five thousand yuan to County Magistrate and Lu Wenmei to urgently produce five thousand sets of cotton clothing to send to the disaster area for the victims to keep warm. The priest of the Tangmuqiao Catholic Church in the county donated one hundred piculs each of white rice and rice to send to the disaster area for emergency relief. Charitable organizations such as the Shanghai Jisheng Association are sending personnel to investigate the dire situation in the disaster area and will likely provide large-scale relief in the future. However, while the victims' basic needs of food and shelter can be temporarily met, it is merely a drop in the bucket. It is hoped that major philanthropists will continue to provide assistance.

Chongming

At six o'clock last night, Chongming gentry Wang Dankui and Chen Ganqing, along with Shanghai natives Lu Wanfu and Wu Bokang, and County Magistrate Shen Jiang, Water Police Captain Long Jinqin, Party Department Supervisor Chen Tiyun, and Property Department Director Tao Zhu, who came to Shanghai to solicit relief, gathered at the Shipping Club on Guangdong Road to discuss relief measures. County Magistrate Shen also solicited donations from major charities and charitable organizations in Shanghai. The Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, in view of the severe rainstorms, hurricanes, and tidal surges that caused the breaches of dikes and embankments, causing widespread flooding, has already dispatched personnel to Chuansha for emergency relief. The Chongming area is also being surveyed on the ground. However, before one wave subsides, another rises. The second typhoon has caused even more severe damage. The reports received are recorded as follows:

Urgent Telegram

County Magistrate Li telegraphed: "The second typhoon has caused countless houses in the disaster area to be swept away. Over ten thousand victims are desperately awaiting relief and are on the verge of death. Please expedite emergency relief to save lives."

Appeal

A public letter from the Shanghai Fellow Villagers Association of Tongzhou, Rugao, Chongming, Hai'an, and Qidong states: "Earlier this month, the typhoon struck, and Qidong, located at the confluence of the river and the sea, suffered particularly severely. Many breaches were caused by huge waves along the northeastern coast and southeastern riverbanks of the county. Seawater poured in, flooding the plains to a depth of several feet, turning them into a marsh. Rice fields were submerged, and the autumn harvest is hopeless. Homes were swept away, and people and livestock were drowned. It is heartbreaking to witness. As the autumn wind intensifies, the victims have no homes to return to and are sleeping in the fields, suffering from hunger and cold. We urgently request that personnel be dispatched to provide emergency relief so that the survivors can return to their homes."

It is reported that representatives from the disaster areas of Chuansha, Chongming, and Nanhui went to solicit relief, and people from the provinces affected by the Yellow River also came to report the disaster situation. How different is it from the scene on the Shanyin Road? Alas, fundraising is difficult, and there are too many demands. It is urgently requested that all sectors show compassion and provide assistance to alleviate this great calamity.

Zhejiang Silk Industry Association Cables Opposition to Autumn Cocoon Tax

Telegraphic Request to Zhejiang Finance Department to Withdraw Order

The Zhejiang Silk Industry Association Joint Association, located in Lianzhu Lane, Aiwenyi Road, this city, yesterday sent a telegram on behalf of the Zhejiang Finance Department, stating that the Hangzhou Zhejiang Provincial Finance Department has received a letter from the silk industry associations of Hangzhou, Wuxing, Jiaxing and other counties, stating that the order to collect cocoon tax and issue permits for the autumn cocoon collection period is impossible to comply with, and requesting an appeal for relief. The function period for the Zhejiang silk industry dental posts is specified as one year, and new posts must be paid for and replaced before the end of April each year. The silk market validity of the cocoon posts on the back covers includes spring, summer, and autumn cocoons. All previous sessions have been processed accordingly. This year, the Construction Department promulgated measures for the management of autumn cocoon industries, prohibiting industry owners from freely renting out, and all industries are under the control of official departments. Industry owners only charge agency baking fees and do not take commissions. Since it is not an operational nature, how can they be held responsible for receiving posts? Moreover, this post donation conflicts with the cocoon industry business tax rate. Now, changing the annual replacement to quarterly replacement is not only unaffordable for the cocoon industry, but also damages the credibility of government orders. The association is a group of silk merchants from the entire province, and should act as a channel. We implore Your Department to quickly withdraw the order to re-impose posts on autumn cocoons, so as to comply with public opinion. Respectfully, Zhejiang Silk Industry Association Joint Association.

Mu Ouchu Discusses Planned Economy and China

The issue of planned economy is needed in this day and age, and is of extreme importance to China today. The lecture by Wu Daquan at the Banking Association has been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. Now, we will seek to record the article (Planned Economy and China) written by Mu Jichu for the people to study.

After the European War, the world economy formed two systems: one is the capitalist economic system, and the other is the socialist economic system. These two economic systems, regardless of their fundamental differences in nature, both tend towards a planned economy. This is an inevitable requirement of history and the times, brewing into the surging new tide of today's era, and is unstoppable. The so-called planned economy, in a nutshell, is the planned control of economic activities of a certain large unit. In socialist countries, it is called (planned economy), while in European and American countries, it is commonly referred to as (planned economy). The term control does not mean arbitrary management and distribution according to private opinions, but a fair, organized, planned, and rational control and command. Its purpose is to improve the economic organization and improve the national economy and people's livelihood. Locke said, (Planned economy is to limit the economic activities of the people and groups to form the scope of action prescribed by the group, and this scope of action is rationally divided, such as cutting and pasting parts into a harmonious whole to achieve the universal social purpose assumed by reason). Lorwin also said, (Planned economy is a system of economic organization in which each individual workshop, enterprise, and industry is regarded as a coordinated unit in a whole, so as to use all available capital to maximize the satisfaction of the needs of a nation during a certain period, and its most important point is that each production unit must rely on this entire system to balance production and consumption). The opposite of planned economy is the economy of laissez-faire competition. The economy of laissez-faire competition has indeed pushed the capitalist economy to the extreme, but today, it is full of drawbacks, and has become the cause of the entire world's increasing decline. The reason is that within the economic scope of laissez-faire competition, whether it is industrial or agricultural production, it is all unplanned production, and it does not seek to be compatible with consumption. Therefore, the significance of planned economy is to evolve the economy of laissez-faire into the economy of controlled economy, and to evolve the economy of free competition into the economy of coordinated action. Today, all countries in the world are vigorously implementing the planned economy movement. Because the current world economic panic is deep, the powers are all working hard to seek to relieve the current predicament. Therefore, politically, they are mostly returning to dictatorship, and economically, they are also moving towards a self-sufficient economic nationalism. The economy of free competition has already shown many flaws, and the planned economy will inevitably replace it. As for the methods of planned economy, they are roughly three categories: one is to exercise the power of strong rule, to take all industries as state-owned, to control the entire economy with the power of the state, and to promote all economic activities with planned action. This is typified by the Soviet Union's planned economy. The second is industrial union, that is, individual entrepreneurs, feeling the pressure of the environment, control the production business of each department separately in a united manner, and make planned activities, and even force entrepreneurs and employees to form an industrial group together to form a social group. The lower level is subject to the full control and domination of the upper level. This method is actually a kind of (cartel) or (trust) internal rationalization movement, and its shortcomings are numerous, and it cannot be regarded as a pure planned economic movement. The third is that the government uses its political management power to make planned control of the people's economic activities. This is different from the Soviet Union's revolutionary method, and it is stronger and more effective than the industrial union method. Therefore, this method is mostly adopted by European and American powers. Germany, France, England, Italy, and Japan all take this method as the principle, and seek to open up the economic panic. That is, the economic recovery movement of the current US President Roosevelt is also based on this as its backbone. Not only that, but today's planned economy movement has evolved into an economic alliance of several countries or a certain federation, such as the British Empire, the American Federation, and Germany are all gatherings, and their federations implement planned economy to form a strong and powerful economic alliance. The famous Ottawa Conference of the British Empire is a clear example. Secondly, Japan (Manchukuo) also has the brewing of the so-called economic alliance. Here, we can all know how the powers are now concentrating all their efforts to seek the opening of the difficult situation of the increasingly serious economic panic. At the same time, we can also know that in today's country, if it cannot implement a planned economy, then its national economy will fall into a state of disorder and cannot be shaken off. It is simply impossible to be listed as a member of the world economy. My country's national economy today is on the verge of total bankruptcy. In terms of industry, all industrial sectors are dying. In terms of agriculture, the entire rural area is devastated, the people's livelihood is ruined, and the foundation of the country is shaken. And due to the economic panic, the surging tide, the powers are now eyeing covetously, and all want to control my country with their huge economic power, so that my country actually falls into the hell of a secondary colony. Therefore, my country is already in the most difficult period. If my country does not prepare to implement a planned economy at this time, and break the current state of economic disorder with planned action, then in the long run, the national lifeline and people's livelihood will be difficult to continue, and the result will inevitably fall into the tragic situation of the economic co-management of the powers. Therefore, the recent proposal by Song Ziwen to implement a planned economy after returning from the World Economic Conference, as well as the central government's recent move to expand the organization of the Economic Commission, should also be regarded as a measure to adapt to the needs of the times and have a refreshing atmosphere. Speaking of implementing a planned economy, we should first understand its prerequisites. What are the prerequisites? That is, (1) there should be a strong and powerful central government, (2) it should be an independent and self-reliant country, (3) there should be accurate investigation and statistics on resources, population, and industrial production figures, (4) there should be capital and technical personnel available for use, (5) there should be precise plans suitable for national conditions. These five are indispensable prerequisites, and especially the first point is more important. For this reason, it is especially difficult for my country to implement a planned economy today. First, my country's central government orders cannot yet reach all provinces, and many remote areas still act arbitrarily. The whole country cannot be united, so once a planned economy is implemented, there will be more resistance. This is one of the obstacles. Second, my country's economy is inherently backward compared to European and American powers. Precisely because of its backwardness, it has almost been completely controlled by European and American powers in recent years. In terms of financial business, the entire control is held by bankers in New York, London, Paris, and Tokyo, which is tantamount to the general hub that dominates the entire national economic life of my country. In terms of transportation, whether it is railways on land, waterways by water, or airways by air, they are almost all monopolized by the powers. I have lost the control of the transportation pulse. In terms of industry, both heavy industry and light industry are also controlled by the capital forces of the powers. Under its high pressure, my country's industries are dying. What is even worse is that today, all countries in the world are doing their best to raise their tariff barriers to prevent the intrusion of foreign goods and protect their domestic industries. Only my country's tariffs have not yet implemented a protection policy. As a result, foreign goods pour in, and rights and interests spill over. The economic power of the powers extends into my country's poor and remote areas. My country's production business is unable to compete with it. If it is not a vassal, it will go bankrupt. If a planned economy is implemented at once, this foreign capital force will inevitably make a strong reaction. This is the second obstacle. Third, in the past, my country's state-owned enterprises were mostly corrupt and unbearable. The state-owned enterprises were called state-owned, but in fact they were mostly controlled by bureaucrats. Their employment administration was unplanned, and they were all ignorant of business common sense. They were only able to invade public funds and enrich their own pockets. Therefore, state-owned enterprises, the content of food, is not worth asking. As for private enterprises, they suffer from the thinness of capital, the burden of taxes, the chaos of turmoil, and the high pressure of foreign capital forces. There are also very few that are relatively large-scale and have a tight organization that is sufficient to be promising. Therefore, today, in terms of planned economy, the shortage of capital, and even the lack of talents, are also major obstacles. This is the third obstacle. Fourth, my country's society has not yet completely broken away from the scope of agricultural economy. The consciousness of farmers is mostly scattered and unorganized. This kind of scattered and unorganized people also have obstacles to the implementation of a planned economy. This is the fourth obstacle. Summarizing the above four points, it can be seen that my country is urgently waiting for the implementation of a planned economy, but in terms of the environment, there are many obstacles, and it is not easy to ignore them. Then, shall we sit back and watch in front of these reefs, and continue to follow the old ways and shrink back? This is absolutely impossible. However, those who fear difficulties are still hindered by difficulties. On the contrary, in the dictionary of those who are brave, resolute, willing to sacrifice and struggle, there is absolutely no word (difficult). My country is rich in resources, and the treasures are piled up like mountains. Nature has given me richness and generosity. Then, if we are willing to devote ourselves to economic transformation with the greatest determination and the spirit of greatest sacrifice, that is, to engage in the implementation of a planned economy, it is also not difficult to reap the greatest benefits. Moreover, my country's planned economy movement, in Dr. Sun Yat-sen's industrial plan, such as developing industry, such as borrowing foreign capital, and technical talents have long been taken into account. We must adhere to his legacy, examine the current environment, study precise plans, and with the most fair and greatest sincerity, overcome obstacles, and do things in a practical way. People make things happen. We must not limit ourselves by difficulties. What is said in this article is a general discussion. Later, we will contribute our views on its theory and implementation plan separately. At the same time, we sincerely hope that my government and my people will all rise up to make practical discussions on this issue.

Xu Shanxiang Speaks on the American Recovery Plan

International Problems Research Association Invites, Only Increasing National Productivity Can Save the Nation

Xinsheng News Agency says, the International Problems Research Association held a tea party for members at the Bank Club at 5 p.m. on the 22nd. They specially invited Mr. Xu Shanxiang, former technical supervisor of the Ministry of Industry, to speak on the American Industrial Recovery Plan. Mr. Xu had just returned to Shanghai from the United States, so he has a deep understanding of the plan. The following is a record of his speech:

I have traveled to the United States three times. The first time was before the European War, when the major railways had just been completed, domestic businesses were proceeding along natural lines, the people lived and worked in peace, and the economy was exceptionally stable. The second time was after the European War, when scientific progress was too rapid, the rich became extremely rich, and industrial expansion was excessive. Stock prices far exceeded their actual value, and the economy gradually showed signs of instability. This trip to the United States was after the Great Depression, when industry and commerce were extremely depressed, and the economy was extraordinarily panicked. This kind of depression phenomenon exists in all countries, but the United States has the most developed industry, so the impact it suffers is also greater than that of other countries. There are roughly four major reasons for the American depression: (1) Industry developed too quickly, resulting in overproduction and supply exceeding demand; (2) War debts were delayed and financial security was stagnant, resulting in weak purchasing power and reduced consumption; (3) American manufactured goods take the world as their market. Now all countries in the world have greatly increased their tariff barriers, and most of the gold-using countries have implemented a virtual gold standard, but the United States is not doing so, resulting in higher prices and inability to compete with others; (4) The invention of a large number of machines has replaced manual labor, resulting in an increasing number of unemployed people. To fundamentally solve this depression problem, it is necessary to rely on the strength of the whole world. The United States, seeing this, held great hope before the opening of the world conference. Secretary of State Hull, on the day of his departure from the United States to England, published an article that roughly stated, (No country in the world can prosper alone. To save the current depression, it is necessary to abandon its closed-door policy and unanimously join the international economic plan, and especially take the reduction of tariff barriers, the stabilization of international exchange rates, and the creation of a standard currency as the three prerequisites. If we follow this path, I know that the prices of major commodities in the world market will naturally increase, and all countries will benefit from it.) The above can represent the psychology of the entire American people. If this goal can be achieved, not only can the American problem be solved, but the depression of the whole world can be eliminated. It is a pity that none of the countries participating in the conference are not selfish and self-interested, and they all want to sacrifice the interests of others without being willing to sacrifice their own interests in the slightest. After the meeting for several weeks, there were no results, and the American depression became more and more serious. Thereupon, President Roosevelt suddenly realized that international empty talk was not to be relied upon, and immediately changed his policy, starting with internal rectification, Put house in order first. He organized the National Recovery Committee, with General Johnson as chairman, and stipulated various industry taxes, inviting the national masses to participate, which is the so-called Blue Eagle Movement. The main purpose of the Blue Eagle Movement is nothing more than the three major principles of increasing wages, reducing working hours, and controlling mass production. According to General Johnson's recent announcement, since the start of the movement, there have been three phenomena: (1) Two million unemployed people have found jobs, and the extra wages paid each week amount to 30 million US dollars. It is expected that 3 million positions can be found before the next Labor Day to settle the unemployed; (2) The government's revenue deficit at the end of last year was 300 million yuan, which can be reduced to 100 million yuan by the end of this year; (3) The 500 million yuan in eight-year government bonds and 350 million yuan in short-term government bonds issued by the government have been sold out, and those who came later even regretted it. This movement is not stipulated in the constitution, but is initiated by the president, requesting the national masses to join unanimously. It is scheduled for a two-year trial period. If the trial is successful, it may be made into law. After the start of the trial, within one year, no matter who is engaged in what occupation, they must obtain a license from the government. Those who join this movement can receive the Blue Eagle sign at the post office after signing and hang it in the store to preside over its affairs. It uses patriotism as its slogan, so even if there are a few people who are not very willing, they have to join. The three letters Z.r.A. originally represent National recovery Aet. (National Recovery Plan), but there are also those who ridicule it as No re- a.an Asked, which is probably the argument of those who are slightly dissatisfied with the government's authoritarianism. The Recovery Committee's plan also has some self-contradictory points. The biggest ones are three: (1) In order to increase grain prices, the government eliminated 15 million acres of cotton fields, subsidizing farmers from 6 to 12 yuan per acre. At the same time, the recovery plan stipulates that 330 million yuan will be used to promote public utilities, a part of which will be used for the completion of the hydropower plan of Muscie Shoals and Boulder Dam. On the one hand, cotton fields are eliminated, and on the other hand, new farmland is irrigated. It is really difficult to implement two steady policies simultaneously; (2) Increasing wages and reducing working hours both increase costs, but purchasing power has not increased in the same way. There is no certainty in terms of sales; (3) Someone has to produce, and someone has to consume. There is still a lot of open space in the central United States that can be reclaimed, but the Red Indians are already extinct, and the white people are not increasing. Immigration is also strictly restricted. Relying solely on the current Americans to consume American products will ultimately not solve the supply and demand problem. Although the recovery plan has various difficulties, there are several points that are very admirable and worthy of our reference: (1) President Luo and his cabinet members have great determination to implement the recovery plan and will not give up despite all setbacks. They act immediately after speaking, so within a few months, they have achieved considerable results, unlike China, which only relies on empty talk on paper, year after year, without accomplishing anything; (2) After the Roosevelt government identifies a policy, it proceeds according to this plan in an orderly manner, unlike China, which is indecisive and changes its orders in the morning and evening; (3) President Roosevelt uses sincere words to inform the public through radio every two or three days. Based on the facts, all the words come from the heart, and the people are moved by them, unlike the Chinese, whose words and actions contradict each other, resulting in the loss of the people's faith; (4) The American people can grant the government considerable power in times of tense situations so that it can act expediently. Even the Republican Party, which opposes the Democratic Party, can sacrifice its political views and support it unanimously. This kind of spirit is indispensable for republican citizens, but the Chinese completely lack it. Although 500 million square miles of territory have been lost and the great enemy is already at the door, internal fighting still occurs every day, fearing that the country will not perish. Because of these four factors, the American recovery undertaking is very promising. I now have the most sincere words to tell the people, that is, within a few years, China will have a very large depression, which will be ten times greater than today. The value of foreign goods imported last year reached more than 89.1 million gold units, and the quantity of native goods exported was only worth more than 41.9 million gold units. The import surplus was about 47.19 million gold units, or 87 million yuan in national currency. Calculated at 400 million people, each person bears about 2 yuan and 20 cents. Judging from China's current situation, the vast majority of people are so poor that they have no place to stand. How can they have the strength to take out 2 yuan per person and send it to foreign countries? It is inevitable that the entire nation will go bankrupt. The American depression is due to overproduction, and the Chinese depression is due to a lack of production. To save the country, there are only seven words: increase national productivity. These seven words were implemented by Mussolini in Italy, turning weakness into strength, and by Stalin in Russia, turning poverty into wealth. The paths taken are different, but the goal is the same. I hope that truly patriotic people will think deeply about this.

Measures for Tax Exemption for Flour Mills Purchasing Wheat

The Municipal Government Has Received an Official Letter from the Ministry of Finance Ordering Compliance

Riri News Agency says that the Ministry of Finance previously received a request from the Shanghai Flour Mill Association to exempt flour mills' branch offices from business tax for selling flour and purchasing wheat. The Ministry held that since wheat flour is subject to a unified tax collected by the central government, provinces and cities should not levy business tax on the manufacturing industry within the scope of the flour mill itself. As for the branch offices or wholesale offices set up by the mills, if they are promoting and selling the flour produced by the mill and have business income, then the branch offices of the mills are neither directly paying the unified tax nor acting as agents for the mill's business of contacting and transferring. They should be taxed according to the business tax of the sales industry. However, after the establishment of the wheat flour tax, the regulations clearly stipulate that the wheat used by each mill as raw material is generally given a tax exemption certificate. Now, the branch offices of each flour mill directly purchase wheat, which is specifically used as the mill's flour-making raw material, which is completely the same in nature as the situation when the mills purchased wheat from various places for flour-making when the wheat flour tax was first established. In order to maintain the central government's wheat flour tax revenue and take into account the commercial difficulties, the Riri News Agency reporter has found and recorded the three items of the approved tax exemption measures for each flour mill's purchase of wheat raw materials as follows: (1) The branch offices of each flour mill must be registered with the Ministry of Industry and directly purchase wheat, which is indeed exclusively for the raw material of the mill's flour-making, and there is no printing behavior. After the competent collection agency verifies that it is consistent, the business tax will be exempted; (2) The offices of each flour mill, in addition to purchasing wheat, should still be taxed according to the business tax if they operate and sell flour and also operate other items; (3) If each flour mill has not established a branch office in the producing area and sends personnel to directly purchase wheat raw materials, the flour mill must be registered with the Ministry of Industry and a certificate is issued by the local Chamber of Commerce, confirming that the purchase is for the use of the mill's raw materials and not for transfer and sale. After the competent collection agency verifies that it is consistent, the business tax should be exempted. Those who have counterfeit factory brands, open branches in the producing area to purchase, or other merchants who operate wheat, in order to prevent selling for profit and taking advantage of loopholes to evade tax, are not within the scope of tax exemption. In addition to consulting with the provincial and municipal governments to order the competent agencies to follow the above measures, the municipal government has received the consultation text yesterday,

Giant Bear Escapes from Municipal Zoo Yesterday Morning

Finally Captured by a Crowd of Workers, but an Old Man Has Been Frightened

Central News Agency says, at about 9:00 a.m. yesterday morning, a large bear suddenly broke free from its lock and escaped from the Municipal Zoo on Wenmiao Road. At that time, a reporter happened to be touring the park, and there were also dozens of other tourists, all of whom were frightened and ran away to avoid it. After the bear escaped, the zoo's administrator hurriedly closed all three gates of the park, temporarily suspending visits in order to capture it. Dozens of people fought the bear, each holding wooden sticks, hemp ropes, and thick iron wires. An old man dressed neatly was caught off guard and could not avoid it. The bear pounced directly on his body, and the old man fell in shock. Fortunately, the bear's teeth had already been removed, so he was not injured, but his clothes were torn by the claws and he was thoroughly frightened. When the pursuers arrived, the bear fled elsewhere. After about half an hour, it was finally surrounded by the park's administrator and workers, some pulling its neck with ropes and others hitting its legs with sticks. The bear finally succumbed and was led back into its cage. The park was reopened as usual after 10:00 a.m.

Wireless Radio Alarm in Cars

In Case of Kidnapping, a Warning Signal Can Be Sent Immediately, the Public Works Department Board Has Approved the Application

During the Public Works Department's regular Wednesday board meeting in the Public Concession, the board approved the Police Committee's suggestion to allow the Wireless Radio Security Company to install wireless radio alarms in cars and cooperate with the police to operate this wireless radio alarm system. According to the company, it has requested a special patent for five years to install receiving radios in police stations and automatic generators in user-owned cars. In case of kidnapping, a warning signal can be sent immediately to report to the police. According to the company's report, the installation of a generator by the user costs between 700 and 1,200 yuan per unit. All expenses for installing and maintaining the receiving radios in the police station and training the patrol police to receive warning signals will be borne by the company. When the Police Committee considered this request, the Chief Inspector reported his support for this move and advocated that if it is necessary to increase personnel in addition to the original personnel in the traffic management room, the company should bear all the expenses. After discussion by the committee, it was decided to recommend to the board that it be allowed to handle it for three years, with all expenses borne by the company, provided that its effectiveness can satisfy the Public Works Department.

Ministry of Communications Orders New Telegraph Machines from England

Kleinschmidt High-Speed Telegraph Machines, Seven Units Worth £13,000, Will Be Shipped to Shanghai at the End of the Month

The telegraph machines used by various telegraph offices in China are all of the English-made Erls and Weston types. Although these machines have a high speed of sending and receiving telegraphs, it is necessary to re-drill holes in the paper when relaying telegraphs, which is a pity. Recently, countries around the world have adopted British-made Kleinschmidt high-speed motors because this machine can save the hand-operated process of drilling and pressing when relaying telegraphs. The Ministry of Communications has ordered seven units from England, worth £13,000. According to the news from the local telegraph office, all the machinery of the telegraph machine has been shipped from England to Shanghai and will arrive at the port at the end of this month. It is also heard that after the telegraph machine is shipped, the Ministry of Communications plans to distribute it to Shanghai, Nanjing, Hankou, Tianjin, Beiping, Qingdao, Yantai, and other telegraph offices.

Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Health Pays Attention to Citizens' Health

丨The South Shanghai Clinic Will Open at the Beginning of Next Month丨

Adopting Scientific Methods for Garbage Disposal, the Plan to Establish a Public Cemetery Continues

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Health will soon establish the South Shanghai Clinic in South Shanghai to facilitate citizens. It will also use scientific methods to handle the garbage problem in the city, and the construction of a public cemetery is also in active progress. The news is recorded separately as follows:

Adding Clinics

The bureau believes that the South Shanghai district has a dense population, and although there are already one or two hospitals, they are still insufficient. Therefore, it has prepared a plan and submitted it to the municipal government to set up another South Shanghai Clinic. The municipal government believes that the bureau's request is indeed needed and has already instructed its approval. It also ordered the Finance Bureau to allocate 4,800 yuan for the establishment of the clinic and stipulated a recurring expense of 1,000 yuan per month. The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Health has received the funds from the Finance Bureau and is actively preparing. In addition to surveying and determining the Yude Lane opposite the old county office on Lai Road as the site of the hospital, various clinical instruments and medicines have also been prepared separately, and physicians have also been hired separately. It is learned that the institute will be officially opened at the beginning of next month.

Garbage Disposal

The Municipal Bureau of Health believes that the issue of garbage disposal in the city is very important to the health of citizens. Therefore, it specially hired Mr. Ma, an engineer, to prepare a plan for garbage disposal in the city based on scientific methods. It is learned that after the implementation of the plan, many of the previous abuses can be eliminated. Among them, the garbage collection of scavengers is no longer based on the size of the area, but on the weight of the collected garbage, stipulating the weight of garbage transported by each person per day to ensure fairness. As for the garbage piling field, it is temporarily still at Longhuazui, as this place can still be used for several years. However, in order to prepare for a rainy day, they are still looking for low-lying areas for future use. In addition, the drainage of ditches in various districts was previously handled by the municipal commissioners' offices in each district, but each district cannot handle it seriously. Currently, the bureau has taken over the districts of Gaoqiao and Pusong, and the results have improved compared with the past. Other districts will also be taken over successively.

Founding a Public Cemetery

The Bureau once established the First Public Cemetery in Jiangwan. However, due to the Ministry of Railways' planned relocation of the railway line, the cemetery site was included within its boundaries, leading to a suspension of the project. Now, the Ministry of Railways, facing financial difficulties, has temporarily shelved the plan. Therefore, the Bureau is now proceeding with it again. Once the cemetery foundation is leveled, the First Public Cemetery can be rented out. A site has also been selected in Beixinjing, but due to limited funds, it is feared that it cannot be realized in the short term. As for taking over the International Cemetery, it is difficult to achieve for the time being.

Mrs. Han questions on what basis the Gold Exchange can determine her husband's death was due to natural causes. This is what the widow cannot understand. As for the Exchange's inadequate facilities, there is no denying it. Now, in order to shield the criminal, they falsely claim her husband suddenly fainted. How can someone faint in a well-ventilated place? Trying to cover up only makes things worse. Judging from the Exchange's letter, it is more than likely that her husband died a violent death. She implores the press to uphold a sense of compassion and reveal the truth of this matter in the newspaper so that everyone knows her husband died a violent death and is not simply dismissed by the Exchange's deceptive words. If so, the living and the dead will be grateful.

Fashion Workers Dismissed and Wages Reduced

Re-igniting the Brewing Labor Unrest

Garment Workers' Union Convenes a Meeting to Discuss Petitioning Party and Government Agencies for Relief and Assistance

There are more than 500 fashion garment workers in this city, working in more than 40 fashion stores throughout the city, specializing in making fashionable women's autumn and winter coats and evening gowns. The wages for each piece range from one yuan and several jiao to more than two yuan. In April of this year, the owners of the industry suddenly announced a reduction of wages of several jiao per piece, citing slow business, which caused dissatisfaction among the workers and led to a strike. Later, the Garment Industry Workers' Union petitioned the Party and government agencies to convene a meeting of both parties for mediation. Four clauses were agreed upon and the original wages were restored, and the labor unrest ended. Later, as the weather gradually warmed up, there was no business for fashionable garments, so the workers of the industry returned to their hometowns for a summer rest, as usual. Unexpectedly, the owners of the industry took the opportunity to greatly increase the number of apprentices and hired unskilled workers to take advantage of their cheap labor and lack of organization. Now that the autumn season has arrived and business is booming, the old workers have returned to the stores to resume their previous work. Unexpectedly, after arriving at the stores, most were rejected and not rehired. Even those who were hired had their wages greatly reduced, even more so than in the spring. This caused great panic among the workers, who reported it to the garment workers' union and convened a general meeting. In addition to petitioning the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Bureau for relief, they are also preparing to take appropriate measures to deal with the situation.

On the 20th of this month, the court approved Jia Lin's request and issued a search warrant, ordering Chinese and Western detectives to go to Lin's hospital to search Lin Xianjian's patient registration book, Jia Lin's luggage, and correspondence between Jia and Lin. However, the search resulted in only one registration book, and the luggage was nowhere to be found. Yesterday morning was the date for the continued hearing of the case. The original plaintiffs and defendants, each accompanied by their lawyers, arrived in court. At 10:45 AM, Judge Feng Shide conducted the hearing. First, Police Lawyer Qian Xunjiu stated the situation of dispatching detectives to Zhenjiang to retrieve the marriage certificate and searching Lin Xianjian's residence. He then presented the certificate and the seized books to the court. The handling detective then reported the process and stated that Ma Fengting, who lives at No. 216 Fusheng Lane, Bazi Road, had been summoned, but he refused to appear in court as a witness. The court then questioned Jia Lin, who stated that on August 26th and 28th of last year, there were patients registered, which showed that Lin Xianjian was still in Shanghai at that time. How could he have gone to Guangdong to get married? Lin Xianjian, upon hearing this, stated that he went to Guangdong on August 19th and returned to Shanghai on August 30th. During this period, Dr. Yang was entrusted to handle the medical practice. Yang is now in Hangzhou and can be summoned for questioning. In addition, the clerk of the Yixing Shipping Ticket Office at No. 89 Gongguan Road can be summoned to prove that he purchased tickets from the office and took a boat to Guangdong. Also, those who came to my hospital for treatment can be summoned to prove that I was not in the hospital at that time and that Dr. Yang treated them on my behalf. However, Jia Lin objected to the witnesses presented by the plaintiff because they were not from the same hometown, that is, relatives. As a result, they criticized each other. The plaintiff then invited his former classmate, Wu Yanglie, who is now studying at Shanghai University, to the court to testify that he had gone to Lin's house to eat wedding banquet on August 24th of last year, but did not witness the wedding ceremony. Subsequently, Cao Lin requested that the photo studio and negatives where the plaintiff presented the photo of her wearing only a bridal gown be investigated in Jieyang. The plaintiff's lawyer, Wu Yu, also provided several suggestions regarding the investigation of evidence. Judge Feng then ordered that the case be adjourned to October 7th for further hearing.

National Telegraph Bureau to Begin Sending and Receiving Social Telegrams

Effective October 1st

According to the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau's business manager, the Ministry of Transportation wants to facilitate the public to send congratulatory telegrams with low fees. Therefore, a type of discounted telegram called social telegrams is created. The regulations were published in various newspapers earlier this month. Now, according to the Ministry's order, starting from the first day of next month, all telegraph bureaus across the country will uniformly start sending and receiving Chinese telegrams with a minimum of 20 characters per telegram, with a fee of 2 fen per character within the same province and 4 fen per character across provinces. Foreign language telegrams will have a minimum of 10 characters, with a fee of 4 fen per character within the same province and 8 fen per character across provinces. Telegrams are limited to congratulatory and condolence phrases and their replies. The telegram header must include the characters Slt (Social Letter telegram), which will also be counted as one character for the fee. It is also said that in European and American countries, sending telegrams for weddings and funerals is considered the highest respect. In recent years, more than 1,000 congratulatory telegrams have been sent each month in this bureau. Westerners in China also send congratulatory telegrams to friends and relatives in the same place for weddings and birthdays. In the past, full fees were required, but starting next month, they can enjoy discounted rates.

Shanghai Art College National Crisis Propaganda Troupe to Hold Exhibitions in Shanghai in Stages

And Prepare for a Second Long-Distance Propaganda Campaign

The Shanghai Art College National Crisis Propaganda Troupe returned from Mongolia at the beginning of the month and went to Beijing last week to hold a Mongolian Border and North China Sketch Exhibition. From the 16th to the 20th, the exhibition opened for five days at the Confucius Temple Library in the capital. More than 50,000 people visited, making it an unprecedented event. The troupe is now returning to Shanghai and will hold exhibitions in stages at the YMCA and the People's Education Center to awaken people in the Southeast to thoroughly understand the truth about the Mongolian border and promote the success of developing the Northwest. It is also learned that the troupe will come to Shanghai soon to prepare tools for the second long-distance propaganda campaign, which includes making large quantities of materials such as large-scale murals, colored picture newspapers, lantern slide propaganda, and propaganda booklets, which are expected to be completed in three weeks. They will depart on the Double Tenth Festival and travel through 18 provinces: Jiangsu, Shandong, Hebei, Shanxi, Chahar, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Gansu, Qinghai, Shaanxi, Sichuan, Hubei, Hunan, Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, Fujian, and Zhejiang, lasting ten months and covering more than 30,000 miles. This trip will still focus on national crisis propaganda, communicate the feelings of the five ethnic groups, break down North-South barriers, and unite the country to resist foreign insults.

Overseas Chinese School's Rental Dispute Involves Litigation in Court

Zhu Qizhao, who resides at No. 609 Continental Market, Nanjing Road, recently leased a piece of land at No. 9514 and 9888 on West Adams Road for a term of 25 years. He then raised funds to build houses, which are now at No. 485 Lane, West Adams Road. However, the construction of these houses required 185,000 taels. Because Zhu did not have this large sum, he mortgaged the land lease contract and the ownership of the rent to the Huizhong Bank for 120,000 taels for a term of ten years, during which the loan would be repaid in twelve installments. At the end of the term, the house would still belong to Zhu Qizhao, and the mortgage would also be cleared. In March of this year, the private Overseas Chinese Middle School wanted to expand its school buildings and saw that the lane was quite suitable. Therefore, it discussed with Zhu Qizhao to purchase the houses, and after several negotiations, the price was agreed upon at 264,200 taels. The contract was also set for ten years, and the payment method was set at 145 installments. The Overseas Chinese Middle School first paid 1,374 taels and 34 cents as the first installment. The Overseas Chinese Middle School believed that since it had invested in purchasing all the rights to the land and houses, the right to collect rent had been transferred to it. When the rent collection period arrived, the Huizhong Bank had already collected the rent. When it inquired with the Huizhong Bank, it replied that it was subject to the mortgage rights. Therefore, the Overseas Chinese Middle School suspected Zhu Qizhao of fraudulent behavior and filed a complaint with the First Special District Court, accusing Zhu of the crime of fraud. Yesterday afternoon, the case was heard in the Fifth Criminal Court. Ma Canhan, the legal representative of the Overseas Chinese Middle School, appeared in court to state the above situation and said that the Overseas Chinese Middle School and the defendant signed a contract (in English, the contract stated that the defendant would transfer the land lease contract and the ownership mortgage contract to the Huizhong Bank to the Overseas Chinese, and the transfer contract also designated the Puyi Bank as its trustee and had full power to fulfill the contract. At the time, the witness in attendance was Huang Zongxun, a representative of the Puyi Company, who agreed that after the transfer contract was signed, he would transfer the Huizhong Bank's mortgage and all contracts to the trustee (that is, Puyi) for safekeeping, and the Overseas Chinese could only recover the contract after the above-mentioned promissory notes were paid off in installments. It also stated that Zhu Qizhao would lease the land and houses to the Overseas Chinese in two sections, A and B, with an annual rent of 12,900 taels for section A and 13,200 taels for section B, for a term of ten years, starting from August 1st of this year. By the beginning of August, the term rent had not been received, and the Huizhong Bank replied that Zhu had no right to transfer, etc. According to Zhu Qizhao, the fact that the house was mortgaged to the Huizhong Bank was clearly stated on the transfer contract, which the informant knew in advance. The Huizhong Bank's reply to the Overseas Chinese also only stated that it was subject to mortgage rights, and did not say that it could not be transferred. The transfer contract stated that the Overseas Chinese must find a guarantor for each installment payment, but the Overseas Chinese did not fulfill this obligation, and the期金 (term payment?) of more than 260,000 was not paid on time. Therefore, the plaintiff himself violated the contract first. At this point, Zhu Qizhao's lawyer, Yuan Yang'an, stated that the content of the case was quite complicated. The contract at the time was in English, and the wording was quite unclear. Once translated, it became even more ambiguous. Even this lawyer spent a lot of time studying the details when he took over the case. As a result, he felt that there was no need for a criminal prosecution in this case. Both parties should pay for the contract. Moreover, Zhu Qizhao had invested 65,000 taels in the land. Although he signed a mortgage contract with Huizhong, if the Overseas Chinese paid the required installments in full, the rent he should receive could be taken away at any time. Therefore, there was no fraud. Moreover, the facts listed in the indictment were inconsistent. Therefore, the details of the case were even more difficult to understand. If the plaintiff could calm down and seek a method of reconciliation, it would be good. Otherwise, he should start with civil matters first and clarify the responsibilities on the contract before speaking. As the case still required clarification of the meaning of the contract and witnesses needed to be questioned, the court was adjourned for further questioning at a later date.

Another Accomplice Arrested in the Case of Chinese and Japanese Conspiring to Rob a Large Sum of Money

Shi Enlian, chief detective of the Hongkou Police Department, and detective Wang Runhe, previously arrested four criminals: Shi Ruichang from Tongzhou, Xu Fengqing from this city, and Japanese nationals Nishi Eiichi and Hosoya Naraju. They seized a pistol and six bullets. It was found that these people had hired a car from the Far East Motor Company at No. 1 Pingliang Road at about 8:00 AM on August 14th, intending to rob passengers of a large sum of money being transported to the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank for storage. While passing the Chinese boundary of Yangshupu near Jun Gong Road, they bound the driver, Hu Songshan, a native of Ningbo, with lead wire, stuffed his mouth with a towel, and threw him by the roadside. A fellow accomplice, Hu Hanshan, drove to the vicinity of the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank on the Bund of Fuzhou Road, waiting for a long time, but the passenger did not arrive. They abandoned the car and fled. The two Japanese were sent to the Japanese Consulate for trial, and Shi and Xu were sent to the First Special District District Court for trial and detention. This has been reported in detail in this newspaper. The detectives handling the case have now arrested another accomplice, Hu Songshan. Yesterday morning, the three criminals, Lu Shi and others, were transferred to the Third Criminal Court of the Special Court. Judge Wu Zehan questioned them. Police Lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that the two Japanese in this case confessed during interrogation at the Japanese Consulate that there was another Japanese accomplice named Takamoto (i.e., Zha Xu Huai La). They had discussed it together in advance at the home of the Japanese Nishi Eiichi. A Chinese man named Xiao Xiang had provided information, claiming that his friend Chen Yongyu had notified Chen that he was working at the Baker Road Commercial Transport Company, but Chen denied being an accomplice. He has now been summoned. The ropes and towels seized by the Fifth District Public Security Bureau were presented for inspection. Chen Yongyu then complained that Xiao Xiang had falsely accused him because he had previously refused to lend him money. When questioned, the defendant Shi Ruichang confessed that he had met three times at the home of the Japanese Nishi Eiichi. Xiao Xiang was indeed present at the time. Hu Hanshan was invited by me to be the driver, but he was very frightened of this kind of thing and did not dare to proceed. Nishi Eiichi said that there would be no problem. Xu Fengqing confessed that Xiao Xiang initiated the matter, claiming that a passenger was planning to deposit a large sum of cash to the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank and informed the Japanese Nishi Eiichi, who asked me to translate Japanese. I did not go with them during the robbery, but waited for news at home. Hu Songshan confessed that he had driven a car in Nantong. Shi Ruichang invited him to discuss the matter. He saw three Japanese men. Later, he went to Far East to hire a car. The car was driven to a remote place in the Chinese area. The Japanese tied up the driver and threw him by the roadside, instructing me to drive to the Bund to rob, but the robbery failed. Finally, Judge Wu instructed the defendants to be returned to custody and set a date for sentencing after a public defender Lin Yangqing was appointed to defend the three defendants.

(11) Member Quan Renfu inquired about the lack of a definite reply after many days regarding the report against Zhu Shengchang for private reconciliation and misappropriation of funds, and whether a reminder letter should be sent.

(12) The Supervisory Committee warned that it is inappropriate to publish in newspapers and execute duties immediately after passing a resolution in a meeting. Thugs Hack Wu Qixing

Wu Qixing, a native of Ningbo, 30 years old, resides in Hongzhen, Pudong. In recent days, he and his friends secretly operated a lottery in Room 32 of the Xizang Hotel on X Z Road. Local thugs discovered this and attempted to extort money from him. Unable to succeed, they harbored a grudge. Yesterday at noon, Wu was enjoying tea at the Yu Ji stove behind the Hua An Insurance Company on Baker Road when suddenly six thugs arrived. Without asking any questions, they brandished axes and hacked at his left foot five times, his right foot once, and his back four times. He immediately bled profusely and lost consciousness. Three New Ghosts in the City of the Wrongfully Dead

Han Chungao Crushed to Death. At 8:35 AM yesterday at the Shanghai South Railway Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, Han Chungao, a 60-year-old man from Taixing, was struck by a No. 44 Shanghai-Longhua train from Longhua Station. He fell onto the tracks, and his head was crushed, causing massive bleeding. He was rushed to Shanghai Hospital, but died at 11:00 AM.

Lin Wangshi Swallows Opium. Wangshi, the 37-year-old wife of Lin Benliang from Anhui, argued with a shoemaker named Wang San near the alley entrance. The wife of Zhou, who lived in the rear room, suddenly helped Wang San and accused Wangshi of impropriety. Unable to vent her anger, Wangshi bought a large amount of opium and committed suicide. She died at midnight.

Cai Xinen Hangs Himself. A young and handsome man wearing a Western suit arrived at a certain hotel on Guizhou Road the day before yesterday afternoon. He rented Room 507 from the hotel, claiming to be Cai Xinen, 20 years old, from Suzhou. Unexpectedly, he used his tie to hang himself on the door. The bookkeeper reported to the old patrol station, and the man was sent to Renji Hospital, but died. A book and a copper watch with a 30th anniversary medal of Soochow University were found in the room. No suicide note or other items were found. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Zhang Junqing arrived to inspect the scene and ordered the body to be collected by the Pushan Villa.

Around 11:30 PM, he returned to the store. The patrol officer rushed to the scene, recorded the car number, and sent the injured man to Renji Hospital. The officer also reported the incident to the patrol station. Yesterday morning, the Traffic Department reported to the Second Special District Court, which assigned the chief prosecutor to the scene. Probably because he wasn't working

Porter Falls into the River and Drowns

He immediately disappeared. His friends hired a salvage boat to search the area. After about two hours, they recovered his body, but he had already drowned. The body was placed on the pier, and the French Concession patrol station notified the water police, who dispatched investigator Gu Zhikui to the scene. It was determined that the deceased was a 33-year-old man from Wuxi nicknamed "Little Wuxi" residing at No. 4 Rensheng Lane, 16th Shed. A woman named Wang Laosan came forward and identified the deceased as her lover and volunteered to prepare a coffin and burial.

Brothel Keeper Sentenced

Zhang Laosan, a brothel keeper from Nanjing who privately opened a brothel in the west wing of No. 4 Dieli Lane, Beijing Road, was recently accused by a prostitute named Teng Xuefang (also known as Aibao) in the First Special Court of forcing her into prostitution and embezzling her jewelry and silver. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu presided over the Second Criminal Court and announced the verdict. Zhang Laosan was sentenced to three months of imprisonment for attempting to profit by enticing a virtuous woman into sexual intercourse with others. Other parts of the charges were acquitted. The associated civil lawsuit was transferred to the court's civil division for trial.

Jiang Hechun Executes Legal Affairs

Mr. Jiang Hechun, a Cantonese, studied law at Meiji University in Japan in his youth. He returned to China in the second year of the Republic and served as a judge in Guangdong for more than ten years. In the nineteenth year of the Republic, he was transferred to the Wenzhou District Court in Zhejiang as a judge, then transferred to the Xiaoshan Court as president, and later appointed by the Ministry as a judge in the Shanghai First Special District Court. Tired of a long official career, he has now established an office at No. 1329 North Sichuan Road to practice law. With his rich academic background and experience, he will surely fulfill his responsibility to protect the people.

Free Talk

Kong Yiji and His Environment

— Wuyou

Regarding Ah Q in "The True Story of Ah Q" (呐喊), some say he is already dead, while others say he is still among us. The debate is widespread and has become a common saying, even for those who specialize in fabricating rumors and attacking Lu Xun. Because Ah Q, as the author said in "How I Started Writing Fiction," "His mouth is in Zhejiang, his face is in Beijing, and his clothes are in Shanxi," is made up of many Chinese bad habits and is inherently universal.

Also in "The True Story of Ah Q" (呐喊), there is a character similar to Ah Q, and that is Kong Yiji. Kong Yiji's characteristics are: first, he is full of classical phrases and quotes (之乎者也), even when talking to children, he says, "Is it much? Not much!" (多乎哉？不多也！). Secondly, he wants to put on a false front. Even though he can only stand and drink with the common laborers, he refuses to take off his long gown, which is dirty and torn and seems to have not been washed or repaired for more than ten years. Thirdly, when he cannot argue with the powerful drinkers and the shopkeeper, he vents his anger on the weak and powerless apprentice and claims competence. This is not much different from Ah Q's spiritual victory method, where he thinks of being beaten as his son beating his father. Kong Yiji, who is lazy and loves to eat (好吃懶做), steals pens, ink, paper, and inkstones when he is hired to copy books. However, he has particularly good credit at the tavern: he wants to share a mere one-penny aniseed snack for drinking with each child; although he is ridiculed everywhere, he takes on the responsibility of teaching the apprentice in the tavern; when he hears people say he is stealing, he blushes and even bursts out with veins to argue, which really makes people feel both angry and funny.

However, Kong Yiji's environment is even more ridiculous. The common laborers and the shopkeeper want to have fun at Kong Yiji's expense. They want to expose his secrets, making him blush with embarrassment. Then they are triumphant and laugh loudly.

Taking pleasure in other people's embarrassment can be said to be anti-empathy! The people of Luzhen (鲁镇), Kong Yiji's environment, are full of this kind of anti-empathy. First, they embarrass Kong Yiji, and then they seek pleasure from his embarrassment. This is how the people of Luzhen live.

Has Kong Yiji and his environment passed away, or do they still exist?

About Hair

— Ma Guoliang

Since two or three years ago, I have noticed that the hair on the top of my head has gradually thinned. Every morning when combing my hair, the comb teeth are always caught with long and short hairs, and the amount that falls out when washing my hair is even more surprising. Until now, what was originally a thick handful of hair has only a thin layer left, just enough to cover the scalp. At first glance, it doesn't seem thin at all, but if you try to look carefully, you will feel that the black hair is like a transparent paper, revealing the entire scalp. The phrase "outwardly strong but inwardly weak" (外强中乾) is the most appropriate description of my hair.

The graying and loss of hair are originally symbols of aging. But I can't admit it, because I am indeed still young. I cherish my hair as much as I cherish my youth. Although it is not entirely for aesthetic reasons, I always feel that, as Sinclair said, "It is a bit depressing to go bald before the age of thirty."

So, in order to prevent hair loss, I have indeed used many methods. Starting with rubbing my scalp with brandy, as the barber taught me, I have tried various Chinese and Western hair growth medicines sold in the market, but the result is still failure. Although the instructions for each medicine swear that it is "miraculously effective" (其效如神). Since God doesn't help me, what else can I do! From the perspective of human beauty, hair is indispensable. At least in today's society, whether a woman has hair or not, just like whether she has a pair of eyes or not, directly affects her happiness in life. Fortunately, I am a man, and there is already the invention of the hat for protection, so even if it loses the last strand, it doesn't matter. I only fear that its loss is of no value.

It is said that there are two types of people who are most prone to hair loss. One type is soldiers, because excessive sweat can damage the hair roots. The other type is politicians, scientists, writers, etc., that is, those who overuse their brains. Aside from the fact that soldiers cannot be equated with myself (because I have not even tried strenuous military exercises), the hair that others lose does indeed have its reasons and values for falling out. But I myself am inexplicably losing hair, which seems a bit presumptuous. Einstein contributed great ideas and scholarship to mankind, and at the age of seventy, he still has a thick head of hair; I am only in my twenties, and I have made no contribution to mankind, yet I have lost a lot of hair. Shouldn't I be ashamed to say so?

I am not a thinker, but my hair is falling out like many thinkers, as if I am ignorantly talking about politics while everyone is cursing me, or talking about national construction plans without understanding the reality of history. It is equally unforgivable. I always hope that there is a medicine, or that I will be given a magical elixir by an immortal in my dream, so that I will not be bald in the future and will have the appearance of an ordinary person. Otherwise, since I am ignorant and incompetent, but pretend to be a thinker, if others misunderstand and mistakenly think that I am a thinker, and mistakenly believe my words and go astray, I really cannot bear the guilt. It would be better to quietly return to the group of the ignorant and let the truly wise men with thoughts and knowledge spread their truth, so as not to confuse people's views and hearing. Then, even though I have made no contribution, I am fortunate not to have destroyed anything from it, and I will be very satisfied.

But where can I find a medicine that can really cure hair loss?

Old Peng's Elegy

It's been a long time since I received a letter from Old Peng, a little strange!

Just returned from the hospital, there was a letter from Mr. W on the table: (Old Peng's stomach ailment flared up, he was hospitalized, a cut was made in his chest, and a hole was dug under his left rib. Luckily, he got through it.) I felt like an electric current ran through my entire body.

Five minutes before twelve o'clock, the postman delivered a letter from Little Chen: (I went to see Old Peng. The doctor said it would take two weeks to determine [the outcome]...) A dark shadow suddenly appeared before my eyes and slowly grew larger.

A letter from Mr. S finally confirmed the terror I had been harboring: (Old Peng is dead! When I went to see him, he was still sleeping in the hospital morgue...)

I will never receive a letter from Old Peng again!

乂乂乂乂

Old Peng liked soccer. On the First Normal School's soccer field, I competed with him for several years, but we never talked face to face. When we met in Beijing in 1924, we only exchanged a few perfunctory greetings. In 1930, I drifted to Shanghai, and because my stomach was causing panic, I found him again in the editorial department of the Commercial Press. By then, he had already entered the Chinese literary scene, and the name (Peng Jiahua) occupied a small place among the authors. It seemed that he showed warm sympathy for me in my wandering, and so we took a step forward in friendship. The raging winds of the times stirred the passion of many young people on the western shore of the Pacific. Old Peng's works also changed with the times. The cries of the working masses and the anxieties of the youth of the times could be found in his sharp pen and the smile floating on his face covered with a thick, dark beard.

乂乂乂乂

The most profound impression was a scene at 乂乂:

(Old Peng is here too!) Mr. L shouted under the window one day, a bitter smile on his face.

(Ah!) I replied.

The section number was called for Ding. I hurriedly rolled up my bedding and followed Section Ding to another room. The first person to welcome me was him:

(I didn't expect we would meet here again!) He laughed heartily.

He was very happy at that time, not worrying about anything except his rotting foot. He usually just made a fuss about food, joked with his roommates, and sometimes played chess. When he was quiet, he sat cross-legged on the bed and chatted with us. (This is life, too ordinary...) He always burned with the torch of hope.

His will, like his beard, no matter how sharp the razor, would grow out again tomorrow after being shaved off today, and it would be more and harder than before.

He hadn't shaved for a long time at that time, and he really looked like Zhong Kui.

(The wind from the cracks) could not stir up sand and waves after all, so he went from hell back to the human world. But his stomach ailment became more and more severe from then on.

乂乂乂乂

Now he is sleeping peacefully by the Huangpu River. On the remnants of foreign shells lies his long-suffering body. If the soul is truly immortal, perhaps he will still see the arrival of the raging tides on the Pacific Ocean.

Lunacharsky's Words

Xu Maoyong (Western, active people, when encountering all kinds of pain, unhappiness, and misfortune, immediately investigate the cause and try to cure it with decisive means. Eastern, passive people, however, poison themselves with anesthetics, or simply immerse themselves in fatalism. The former realistically eliminates the difference in life, while the latter covers their eyes to the difference in life, pretends to be indifferent, and narrows the scope of consciousness.)

Lunacharsky said so. (See "On Art")

(Life difference) refers to all the facts that (always subject life to some restrictions and dangers), that is, (give life obstacles).

The rich have fine wine and women; the poor resign themselves to fate. Today, the scope of consciousness of the Chinese people is so narrow that they don't even think of using active means to maintain their own survival, let alone other things – nation and country!

Looking at Japan, which is also (Eastern), although it is unreasonably violent, it is actually also terrified by the difference in life. However, compared to us, they have taken decisive measures. Aren't all their actions erupting under the slogans of (national crisis) and (extraordinary times)? Of course, in our view, their means are a bit too active.

I don't want to say more. I will still quote a passage from Lunacharsky:

(If a race invades the territory occupied by another race and life becomes difficult, then,

The natives can resist and fight; but they can also be content with peaceful and weak survival, submit to fate, leave their homeland, flee to remote and barren lands, and occupy the position of servants. As a result, they gradually become accustomed to insufficient nutrition and food, and their development can also shrink. (Adapted from Lu Xun's translation) Perhaps future historians will borrow this ready-made passage as the conclusion of Chinese history.

Stimulation (3)

— Xie Bingying

An unexpected phone call came. It was from a friend I hadn't seen in seven years since we parted in Wuhan. He came from Guangdong and arrived in Gutian today. He insisted that I go see him. At first, I firmly refused, but later I hesitated a bit because of what he said, such as "the opportunity is rare, and I don't know if we will have a chance to meet again in the future." In this year, my friends are decreasing day by day, and no one knows when anyone will die. It's good to have a chance to meet and talk a few more words while we are alive. Thinking of this, I agreed.

Although I have a horse, it's too hot, and it's not worth it to run twenty li after all. My selfishness is wavering again.

In the end, I decided to go!

It was 2 p.m. Just as I was getting ready to leave, a phone call suddenly came saying that my friend might leave this afternoon, telling me not to go.

So I got annoyed again!

Annoyed, annoyed, annoyed, a thousand times annoyed!

Boom, boom, boom, boom, oh, thunder rumbled, lightning flashed, torrential rain poured down, and a strong wind blew violently. The doors and windows rattled and clattered, the teacups, oil lamps, and teapots on the table rolled to the ground and shattered, and books and newspapers flew all over the room. The torrential rain poured in through the windows, and the whole room was full of water. The rain from the tiled roof soaked the quilts and pillows, and I couldn't even open my eyes. Running out of the room, the raindrops hit my head like iron sheets, causing severe pain, and my clothes were also soaked. The raindrops on my hair fell like beads one by one.

(Oh, no, my books, bedding, and clothes are all wet!)

(Alas! I really didn't expect such a heavy rain. My house is also a mess!)

(You haven't seen it yet, my house is simply like an ocean!)

Hahaha, hearing what they said, I jumped up with joy! Carelessly, my right foot slipped, and I almost fell.

(This rain is really refreshing, now I'm not sad anymore!)

From the moment the storm came, until this moment—9:20 p.m.—my heart is calm, happy, active, and has found endless comfort. (The End)
